Mr. President, the Framers of the Constitution gave the executive branch of our Government authority to provide for the payment of debts incurred by the executive branch of our Government. They set aside the power to levy taxes in general as unconstitutional. President Lincoln followed in their footsteps, signed into law the 13th Amendment to the Constitution.  In the intervening years since, there have been efforts to insert or modify this constitutional amendment, among them at the State level, and at the Federal level. Those efforts have been met with an unrelenting public opinion campaign, and a continuing determination to repeal it. While the Framers of the Constitution believed in congressional control of the purse strings, so did their detractors.  This week, we hope to make amends with this Nation's Constitution by extending the concept of congressional control over the payment of Federal debt.
